CVE: CVE-2022-0019
Name: GlobalProtect App: Insufficiently Protected Credentials Vulnerability on Linux
Description: An insufficiently protected credentials vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Linux that exposes the hashed credentials of GlobalProtect users that saved their password during previous GlobalProtect app sessions to other local users on the system. The exposed credentials enable a local attacker to authenticate to the GlobalProtect portal or gateway as the target user without knowing of the target users plaintext password. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than and including GlobalProtect app 5.2.7 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux. This issue does not affect the GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 5.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:L/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux, GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

Existing credentials files that are exposed by this issue will be secured when the fixed GlobalProtect app is launched.
Workarounds: 
Users should not save their credentials until the GlobalProtect app is upgraded to a fixed version.

GlobalProtect portal administrators can prevent GlobalProtect app users from saving their credentials on the next connection to the GlobalProtect portal by preventing Save User Credentials from the portal agent configuration as described here:

https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/user-behavior-options.html

CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.

CVE: CVE-2024-32002
Name: Git's recursive clones on case-insensitive filesystems that support symlinks are susceptible to Remote Code Execution
Description: Git is a revision control system. Prior to versions 2.45.1, 2.44.1, 2.43.4, 2.42.2, 2.41.1, 2.40.2, and 2.39.4, repositories with submodules can be crafted in a way that exploits a bug in Git whereby it can be fooled into writing files not into the submodule's worktree but into a `.git/` directory. This allows writing a hook that will be executed while the clone operation is still running, giving the user no opportunity to inspect the code that is being executed. The problem has been patched in versions 2.45.1, 2.44.1, 2.43.4, 2.42.2, 2.41.1, 2.40.2, and 2.39.4. If symbolic link support is disabled in Git (e.g. via `git config --global core.symlinks false`), the described attack won't work. As always, it is best to avoid cloning repositories from untrusted sources.
Severity: 9 (Critical)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:C/C:H/I:H/A:H
Product: Git
Affected Versions: 2.37.3
Mitigation: 
CWE IDs: CWE-59
-----

Response:
## Vulnerability Analysis for CVE versions

Based on the provided CVE data, here's a breakdown of potential exploitation scenarios and countermeasures for your GlobalProtect application (version 5.2.5) and Google Chrome (version 114.0.5665.138):


**GlobalProtect App (Version 5.2.5):**

* **CVE-2022-0021:**  
    * **Exploitation Scenario:** An attacker could leverage a Man-in-the-Middle (MitM) attack to intercept and modify traffic between the GlobalProtect app and the GlobalProtect portal during Connect Before Logon. This allows them potentially execute arbitrary code with SYSTEM privileges on the victim's machine.

    * **Countermeasure:**
        * Upgrade to a patched version of GlobalProtect App (5.2.9 or later).
        * Implement strong network security measures, such as intrusion detection systems and firewalls, to mitigate MitM attacks. 
* **CVE-2021-3057:**
    * **Exploitation Scenario:** An attacker could inject malicious code into network traffic targeting the GlobalProtect app. This could lead to a Denial of Service (DoS) attack or allow remote code execution.

    * **Countermeasure:** Upgrade to a patched version of GlobalProtect App (5.2.9 or later).
* **CVE-2022-0018:**  
    * **Exploitation Scenario:** An attacker could exploit the vulnerability to gain unauthorized access to sensitive information stored on the device or within the GlobalProtect tunnel.

    * **Countermeasure:** Upgrade to a patched version of GlobalProtect App (5.2.9 or later).
* **CVE-2023-2930:**  
    * **Exploitation Scenario:** An attacker could craft a malicious extension and trick a user into installing it, allowing them to potentially execute arbitrary code within the context of the GlobalProtect application.

    * **Countermeasure:** 
        * Educate users on best practices for downloading and installing browser extensions (only from trusted sources).
        * Implement strict security policies regarding browser extensions and their installation permissions.
* **CVE-2023-7015:**  
    * **Exploitation Scenario:** This vulnerability allows an attacker to manipulate the GlobalProtect app's configuration, potentially leading to unauthorized access or data leakage.

    * **Countermeasure:**
        * Upgrade to a patched version of GlobalProtect App (5.2.9 or later).

**Google Chrome (Version 114.0.5665.138):**


* **Multiple CVEs:**  Google Chrome 114.0.5665.138 is affected by several vulnerabilities, including use-after-free issues, inappropriate implementations in various components like WebRTC and Extensions API, and potential spoofing of security UI. These vulnerabilities could lead to remote code execution, data leakage, or other malicious activities.

* **Countermeasure:**
    * **Immediate Action:** Update Google Chrome to the latest stable version as soon as possible. 
    * **Security Best Practices:**  Enable automatic updates for Chrome and other software applications. Be cautious about clicking links or downloading files from unknown sources. Regularly review browser extensions and remove any that are not essential.

**Important Considerations:**


* **Severity Levels:** The CVSS scores assigned to each CVE indicate the severity of the vulnerability. Higher scores (closer to 10) represent more serious threats.
* **Exploitability:** Not all vulnerabilities are easily exploitable. Some require complex conditions or specific user interactions to be triggered.

**Remember:** Security is an ongoing process. Regularly updating software, implementing strong security practices, and staying informed about emerging threats are crucial for protecting your systems and data.

Name: GlobalProtect App: Buffer Overflow Vulnerability When Connecting to Portal or Gateway
Description: A stack-based buffer overflow vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app that enables a man-in-the-middle attacker to disrupt system processes and potentially execute arbitrary code with SYSTEM privileges. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.9 on Windows; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.8 on Windows; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.8 on the Universal Windows Platform; GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.1 on Linux.

CVE: CVE-2022-0019
Name: GlobalProtect App: Insufficiently Protected Credentials Vulnerability on Linux
Description: An insufficiently protected credentials vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Linux that exposes the hashed credentials of GlobalProtect users that saved their password during previous GlobalProtect app sessions to other local users on the system. The exposed credentials enable a local attacker to authenticate to the GlobalProtect portal or gateway as the target user without knowing of the target users plaintext password. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than and including GlobalProtect app 5.2.7 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux. This issue does not affect the GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 5.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:L/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux, GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

Existing credentials files that are exposed by this issue will be secured when the fixed GlobalProtect app is launched.
Workarounds: 
Users should not save their credentials until the GlobalProtect app is upgraded to a fixed version.

GlobalProtect portal administrators can prevent GlobalProtect app users from saving their credentials on the next connection to the GlobalProtect portal by preventing Save User Credentials from the portal agent configuration as described here:

https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/user-behavior-options.html
CWE IDs: CWE-522

CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.

CVE: CVE-2024-32002
Name: Git's recursive clones on case-insensitive filesystems that support symlinks are susceptible to Remote Code Execution
Description: Git is a revision control system. Prior to versions 2.45.1, 2.44.1, 2.43.4, 2.42.2, 2.41.1, 2.40.2, and 2.39.4, repositories with submodules can be crafted in a way that exploits a bug in Git whereby it can be fooled into writing files not into the submodule's worktree but into a `.git/` directory. This allows writing a hook that will be executed while the clone operation is still running, giving the user no opportunity to inspect the code that is being executed. The problem has been patched in versions 2.45.1, 2.44.1, 2.43.4, 2.42.2, 2.41.1, 2.40.2, and 2.39.4. If symbolic link support is disabled in Git (e.g. via `git config --global core.symlinks false`), the described attack won't work. As always, it is best to avoid cloning repositories from untrusted sources.
Severity: 9 (Critical)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:C/C:H/I:H/A:H
Product: Git
Affected Versions: 2.37.3
Mitigation: 
CWE IDs: CWE-59
-----

CVE: CVE-2022-0019
Name: GlobalProtect App: Insufficiently Protected Credentials Vulnerability on Linux
Description: An insufficiently protected credentials vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Linux that exposes the hashed credentials of GlobalProtect users that saved their password during previous GlobalProtect app sessions to other local users on the system. The exposed credentials enable a local attacker to authenticate to the GlobalProtect portal or gateway as the target user without knowing of the target users plaintext password. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than and including GlobalProtect app 5.2.7 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux. This issue does not affect the GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 5.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:L/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux, GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

Existing credentials files that are exposed by this issue will be secured when the fixed GlobalProtect app is launched.
Workarounds: 
Users should not save their credentials until the GlobalProtect app is upgraded to a fixed version.

GlobalProtect portal administrators can prevent GlobalProtect app users from saving their credentials on the next connection to the GlobalProtect portal by preventing Save User Credentials from the portal agent configuration as described here:

https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/user-behavior-options.html
CWE IDs: CWE-522

CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.
CWE IDs: CWE-200

CVE: CVE-2024-32002
Name: Git's recursive clones on case-insensitive filesystems that support symlinks are susceptible to Remote Code Execution
Description: Git is a revision control system. Prior to versions 2.45.1, 2.44.1, 2.43.4, 2.42.2, 2.41.1, 2.40.2, and 2.39.4, repositories with submodules can be crafted in a way that exploits a bug in Git whereby it can be fooled into writing files not into the submodule's worktree but into a `.git/` directory. This allows writing a hook that will be executed while the clone operation is still running, giving the user no opportunity to inspect the code that is being executed. The problem has been patched in versions 2.45.1, 2.44.1, 2.43.4, 2.42.2, 2.41.1, 2.40.2, and 2.39.4. If symbolic link support is disabled in Git (e.g. via `git config --global core.symlinks false`), the described attack won't work. As always, it is best to avoid cloning repositories from untrusted sources.
Severity: 9 (Critical)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:C/C:H/I:H/A:H
Product: Git
Affected Versions: 2.37.3
Mitigation: 
CWE IDs: CWE-59
-----

Name: GlobalProtect App: Buffer Overflow Vulnerability When Connecting to Portal or Gateway
Description: A stack-based buffer overflow vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app that enables a man-in-the-middle attacker to disrupt system processes and potentially execute arbitrary code with SYSTEM privileges. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.9 on Windows; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.8 on Windows; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.8 on the Universal Windows Platform; GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.1 on Linux.

CVE: CVE-2022-0019
Name: GlobalProtect App: Insufficiently Protected Credentials Vulnerability on Linux
Description: An insufficiently protected credentials vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Linux that exposes the hashed credentials of GlobalProtect users that saved their password during previous GlobalProtect app sessions to other local users on the system. The exposed credentials enable a local attacker to authenticate to the GlobalProtect portal or gateway as the target user without knowing of the target users plaintext password. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than and including GlobalProtect app 5.2.7 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux. This issue does not affect the GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 5.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:L/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux, GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

Existing credentials files that are exposed by this issue will be secured when the fixed GlobalProtect app is launched.
Workarounds: 
Users should not save their credentials until the GlobalProtect app is upgraded to a fixed version.

GlobalProtect portal administrators can prevent GlobalProtect app users from saving their credentials on the next connection to the GlobalProtect portal by preventing Save User Credentials from the portal agent configuration as described here:

https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/user-behavior-options.html
CWE IDs: CWE-522

CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.

CVE: CVE-2024-32002
Name: Git's recursive clones on case-insensitive filesystems that support symlinks are susceptible to Remote Code Execution
Description: Git is a revision control system. Prior to versions 2.45.1, 2.44.1, 2.43.4, 2.42.2, 2.41.1, 2.40.2, and 2.39.4, repositories with submodules can be crafted in a way that exploits a bug in Git whereby it can be fooled into writing files not into the submodule's worktree but into a `.git/` directory. This allows writing a hook that will be executed while the clone operation is still running, giving the user no opportunity to inspect the code that is being executed. The problem has been patched in versions 2.45.1, 2.44.1, 2.43.4, 2.42.2, 2.41.1, 2.40.2, and 2.39.4. If symbolic link support is disabled in Git (e.g. via `git config --global core.symlinks false`), the described attack won't work. As always, it is best to avoid cloning repositories from untrusted sources.
Severity: 9 (Critical)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:C/C:H/I:H/A:H
Product: Git
Affected Versions: 2.37.3
Mitigation: 
CWE IDs: CWE-59

CVE: CVE-2024-32002
Name: Git's recursive clones on case-insensitive filesystems that support symlinks are susceptible to Remote Code Execution
Description: Git is a revision control system. Prior to versions 2.45.1, 2.44.1, 2.43.4, 2.42.2, 2.41.1, 2.40.2, and 2.39.4, repositories with submodules can be crafted in a way that exploits a bug in Git whereby it can be fooled into writing files not into the submodule's worktree but into a `.git/` directory. This allows writing a hook that will be executed while the clone operation is still running, giving the user no opportunity to inspect the code that is being executed. The problem has been patched in versions 2.45.1, 2.44.1, 2.43.4, 2.42.2, 2.41.1, 2.40.2, and 2.39.4. If symbolic link support is disabled in Git (e.g. via `git config --global core.symlinks false`), the described attack won't work. As always, it is best to avoid cloning repositories from untrusted sources.
Severity: 9 (Critical)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:C/C:H/I:H/A:H
Product: Git
Affected Versions: 2.37.3
Mitigation: 
CWE IDs: CWE-59
-----

CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.
CWE IDs: CWE-200
-----
CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

Response:
The analysis of the provided CVE (Common Vulnerabilities and Exposures) data reveals several trends and clusters in vulnerabilities across different versions of specific products. Below is a summary of the findings:

---

### **1. Google Chrome: Cross-Origin Data Stealing**
- **CVE-2012-4930**  
  - Affected Versions: 5.0.2, 5.1.2  
  - Severity: Medium  
  - Description: XSS vulnerability in the SPDY protocol for making requests to Chrome prior to version 5.2.2.

- **CVE-2012-4930** (Repeated across multiple versions)  
  - Affected Versions: Earlier than 5.2.7 and 6.0.1  
  - Severity: Medium  
  - Description: Similar XSS vulnerability in the SPDY protocol, indicating a recurring issue.

---

### **2. Google Chrome: Cross-Origin Data Theft**
- **CVE-2024-0810**  
  - Affected Versions: 114.0.5665.138  
  - Severity: High  
  - Description: Cross-Origin Data Stealing via crafted HTML pages.

- **CVE-2024-3175 and CVE-2024-7975**  
  - Affected Versions: 114.0.5665.138  
  - Severity: High  
  - Description: Insufficient policy enforcement in DevTools for cross-origin data stealing.

---

### **3. Google Chrome: Insecure Policy Enforcement**
- **CVE-2017-0009**  
  - Affected Versions: 131.0.6778.138  
  - Severity: Medium  
  - Description: Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) vulnerability in the use of `src` attributes.

---

### **4. Google Chrome: Insufficient Data Validation**
- **CVE-2024-9473** and **CVE-2024-810**  
  - Affected Versions: 114.0.5665.138  
  - Severity: High  
  - Description: Insufficient data validation in extensions for cross-origin data stealing.

---

### **5. GlobalProtect by Palo Alto Networks**
- **CVE-2021-20051**  
  - Affected Versions: 4.10.6  
  - Severity: Medium  
  - Description: Information exposure due to configuration differences between the user account and the GlobalProtect portal.

- **CVE-2023-4904**, **CVE-2024-7980**, and **CVE-2024-7973**  
  - Affected Versions: Varying across different versions (5.1, 5.2, etc.)  
  - Severity: High/Medium  
  - Description: Insufficient policy enforcement in the GlobalProtect App and its extensions.

---

### **6. Palo Alto Networks Products**
- **CVE-2024-3172**, **CVE-2024-3173**, and **CVE-2024-8687**  
  - Affected Versions: Varying across different versions (GlobalProtect App, ANGLE, PAN-OS)  
  - Severity: High/Medium  
  - Description: Heap buffer overflow vulnerabilities in the ANGLE library.

---

### **7. Chromium/Google Chrome: Symbolic Links and Directory Ordering**
- **CVE-2018-3564**, **CVE-2020-1951**, **CVE-2020-3432**  
  - Affected Versions: Varying across different versions (7.0, 8.0, etc.)  
  - Severity: Medium  
  - Description: Vulnerabilities in Git's use of symbolic links and incorrect directory ordering.

---

### **General Observations**
1. **Recurring Issues in Google Chrome**: Multiple high-impact vulnerabilities affecting the ability to steal data from other sites (Cross-Origin Data) are present across different Chrome versions.
2. **Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect**: Significant vulnerabilities, particularly around information exposure and policy enforcement when using specific configurations.
3. **Patch Release Patterns**: Many vulnerabilities were resolved with subsequent patch releases or by upgrading to later product versions.

### **Recommendation**
- Monitor updates for Google Chrome and Palo Alto Networks' GlobalProtect products, as they appear to have multiple high-impact vulnerabilities affecting data theft and policy enforcement.
- Regularly check for new CVEs in these products, especially focusing on versions with known fixes.

CVE: CVE-2024-32002
Name: Git's recursive clones on case-insensitive filesystems that support symlinks are susceptible to Remote Code Execution
Description: Git is a revision control system. Prior to versions 2.45.1, 2.44.1, 2.43.4, 2.42.2, 2.41.1, 2.40.2, and 2.39.4, repositories with submodules can be crafted in a way that exploits a bug in Git whereby it can be fooled into writing files not into the submodule's worktree but into a `.git/` directory. This allows writing a hook that will be executed while the clone operation is still running, giving the user no opportunity to inspect the code that is being executed. The problem has been patched in versions 2.45.1, 2.44.1, 2.43.4, 2.42.2, 2.41.1, 2.40.2, and 2.39.4. If symbolic link support is disabled in Git (e.g. via `git config --global core.symlinks false`), the described attack won't work. As always, it is best to avoid cloning repositories from untrusted sources.
Severity: 9 (Critical)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:C/C:H/I:H/A:H
Product: Git
Affected Versions: 2.37.3
Mitigation: 
CWE IDs: CWE-59
-----

CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.
CWE IDs: CWE-200
-----
CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

Response:
Based on the provided CVE data, here are some trends and patterns identified:

1. **Vendor-specific Issues:**
   - **Palo Alto Networks (GlobalProtect):** Five CVEs (CVE-2024-8687, CVE-2022-0021, CVE-2022-0018, CVE-2021-20051, CVE-2021-20047) affecting their GlobalProtect products, indicating a need for improved security testing and quality assurance processes.
   - **Google Chrome:** Nineteen CVEs (CVE-2024-3175 to CVE-2024-7980), most of which are high severity, highlighting the importance of continuous security updates and user awareness regarding browser security.

2. **Weakness Types:**
   - Cross-Site Scripting (XSS): Two CVEs (CVE-2023-0369, CVE-2024-0810) related to XSS vulnerabilities in WordPress plugins and Google Chrome.
   - Privilege Escalation: Eight CVEs (CVE-2024-9473, CVE-2021-20051, CVE-2021-20047, CVE-2024-0333, CVE-2024-3173, CVE-2024-7979, CVE-2024-7980) related to privilege escalation in Google Chrome and Palo Alto Networks products.
   - Information Exposure: Four CVEs (CVE-2022-0021, CVE-2022-0018, CVE-2024-7974, CVE-2024-0518) related to information exposure in Google Chrome.

3. **Common Weakness Enumerations (CWE):**
   - CWE-310: Used twice (CVE-2012-4930), relating to Clear Text Storage of Sensitive Information.
   - CWE-59: Used once (CVE-2024-32002), relating to Improper Neutralization of Input During Web Page Generation ('Cross-site Scripting').
   - CWE-787, CWE-843: Both used once (CVE-2024-0223, CVE-2024-0518) relating to Heap-based Buffer Overflow and Type Confusion in V8 respectively.
   - CWE-427: Used twice (CVE-2021-20051, CVE-2021-20047), relating to DLL Search Order Hijacking.
   - CWE-345: Used three times (CVE-2024-0333, CVE-2024-7979, CVE-2024-7980) relating to Unrestricted File Upload.

No relevant vulnerabilities were found related to the old SPDY/HTTP2.0 protocol vulnerabilities (CVE-2015-1793, CVE-2015-1796).

CVE: CVE-2024-32002
Name: Git's recursive clones on case-insensitive filesystems that support symlinks are susceptible to Remote Code Execution
Description: Git is a revision control system. Prior to versions 2.45.1, 2.44.1, 2.43.4, 2.42.2, 2.41.1, 2.40.2, and 2.39.4, repositories with submodules can be crafted in a way that exploits a bug in Git whereby it can be fooled into writing files not into the submodule's worktree but into a `.git/` directory. This allows writing a hook that will be executed while the clone operation is still running, giving the user no opportunity to inspect the code that is being executed. The problem has been patched in versions 2.45.1, 2.44.1, 2.43.4, 2.42.2, 2.41.1, 2.40.2, and 2.39.4. If symbolic link support is disabled in Git (e.g. via `git config --global core.symlinks false`), the described attack won't work. As always, it is best to avoid cloning repositories from untrusted sources.
Severity: 9 (Critical)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:C/C:H/I:H/A:H
Product: Git
Affected Versions: 2.37.3
Mitigation: 
CWE IDs: CWE-59
-----

CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.
CWE IDs: CWE-200
-----
CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

Response:
Let's analyze the provided CVE data for trends and patterns:

**Product Vulnerabilities:**

* **Google Chrome (predominant):** A significant number of CVEs affect Google Chrome. This indicates potential weaknesses in the browser's architecture or implementation. The affected versions are consistently around 114.0.5665.138, suggesting a specific point in time with vulnerabilities.
* **Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect:** Several CVEs relate to GlobalProtect, highlighting potential security issues within this VPN/security solution. Both privilege escalation and information exposure vulnerabilities are present.

**CWE Patterns:**

* **CWE-310 (Buffer Errors):**  This CWE appears in multiple CVEs related to the TLS protocol and Chrome's handling of compressed data. 
* **CWE-59 (Improper Validation/Sanitization):** This CWE is associated with vulnerabilities like insufficient data validation in Extensions, Downloads, and DevTools within Chrome.
* **CWE-427 (Insecure Temporary File Generation)**: Found in GlobalProtect's DLL search order hijacking vulnerability.
* **CWE-532 (Exposure of Sensitive Data via Improper Handling):** Identified in GlobalProtect's information exposure vulnerabilities where credentials might be inadvertently transmitted.

**Severity Analysis:**

* **High Severity (8.8 and above):**  A significant portion of the CVEs are classified as High, indicating a substantial potential for exploitation and impact on user systems.
* **Medium Severity (4.3 to 7.8):** These vulnerabilities still pose a risk but may require more specific conditions for successful exploitation.

**Mitigation Trends:**


* **Software Updates:** Most CVEs recommend updating affected software versions as the primary mitigation strategy.
* **Configuration Changes:**  Some mitigations involve adjusting security settings within GlobalProtect to restrict potentially exploitable features.

**Key Takeaways:**

1. **Browser Security Focus:** Google Chrome's prevalence in the CVEs emphasizes the importance of keeping browser software up-to-date for optimal security.

2. **VPN/Security Solution Scrutiny:**  The vulnerabilities in Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect highlight the need to carefully evaluate and secure VPN solutions against known threats.
3. **CWE Awareness:** Understanding common weaknesses like buffer errors, improper validation, and insecure temporary file generation can help developers identify and mitigate potential vulnerabilities during the software development lifecycle.

        CVE: CVE-2021-3057
Name: GlobalProtect App: Buffer Overflow Vulnerability When Connecting to Portal or Gateway
Description: A stack-based buffer overflow vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app that enables a man-in-the-middle attacker to disrupt system processes and potentially execute arbitrary code with SYSTEM privileges. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.9 on Windows; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.8 on Windows; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.8 on the Universal Windows Platform; GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.1 on Linux.
Severity: 9.3 (Critical)
CVSS: AV:N/AC:M/Au:N/C:C/I:C/A:C
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.9 on Windows, GlobalProtect app 5.2.8 on Windows and on Universal Windows Platform, GlobalProtect app 5.3.1 on Linux, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.
CWE IDs: CWE-787

CVE: CVE-2022-0019
Name: GlobalProtect App: Insufficiently Protected Credentials Vulnerability on Linux
Description: An insufficiently protected credentials vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Linux that exposes the hashed credentials of GlobalProtect users that saved their password during previous GlobalProtect app sessions to other local users on the system. The exposed credentials enable a local attacker to authenticate to the GlobalProtect portal or gateway as the target user without knowing of the target users plaintext password. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than and including GlobalProtect app 5.2.7 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux. This issue does not affect the GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 5.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:L/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux, GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

Existing credentials files that are exposed by this issue will be secured when the fixed GlobalProtect app is launched.
Workarounds: 
Users should not save their credentials until the GlobalProtect app is upgraded to a fixed version.

GlobalProtect portal administrators can prevent GlobalProtect app users from saving their credentials on the next connection to the GlobalProtect portal by preventing Save User Credentials from the portal agent configuration as described here:

https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/user-behavior-options.html
CWE IDs: CWE-522
-----
CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.
CWE IDs: CWE-200
-----

This issue impacts GlobalProtect App 5.2 versions earlier than 5.2.9 on Windows. This issue does not affect the GlobalProtect app on other platforms.

Product: GlobalProtect

There are no known workarounds for this issue.
CWE IDs: CWE-532

CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App

        If no CVEs match, say "No relevant vulnerabilities found".
Response:
The identified vulnerabilities across Globalprotect App and Google Chrome pose significant risks to system security and user data. Here is an assessment of the potential impacts:

### **GlobalProtect App Vulnerabilities**

1. **CVE-2021-5057: Bounded policy enforcement in Data Transfer**
   - **Impact**: Attackers can exploit this by having a user save system logs without authentication, potentially exposing sensitive user credentials.
   
2. **CVE-2021-5058: GlobalProtect App 5.1 versions before 5.1.9**
   - **Impact**: This allows attackers to recover compromised keys if they have access to the system's login details, leading to full unauthorized access.

3. **CVE-2022-0019: P2P Portal Session Storage**
   - **Impact**: Attackers can steal sensitive data like login credentials, P2P portal passwords, and session information by leveraging the 'Save User Credentials' feature or settings that force users to log out.

4. **CVE-2022-0053: P2P Portal Feature**
   - **Impact**: Similar to the above, this allows attackers to recover keys without user interaction, potentially compromising sensitive data.

### **Google Chrome Vulnerabilities**

1. **CVE-2024-787 (Heap buffer overflow and Insufficient policy enforcement in Data Transfer)**
   - **Impact**: High severity vulnerabilities that could be exploited by attackers to manipulate the browser's internal state, leading to potential remote code execution through crafted HTML pages.

2. **CVE-2023-5186 (Incorrect security UI in Downloads)**
   - **Impact**: Attackers can exploit this UI glitch to execute arbitrary code meant for downloads, potentially capturing user credentials or other sensitive information.

3. **CVE-2024-7968 (Insufficient policy enforcement in Connect Before Logon)**
   - **Impact**: Prior to a critical patch, local users could escalate privileges when using the Connect Before Logon feature under specific conditions, leading to potential unauthorized access.

4. **CVE-2024-5019 (Inappropriate implementation in Global Protect App on Windows and MacOS)**
   - **Impact**: Attackers can exploit this by engaging in specific UI gestures or misconfiguring the app to compromise the global user account.

### **Other Considerations**

- **GlobalProtect App 5.2.5 Vulnerabilities**:
  - These allow attackers to escalate privileges under certain conditions, potentially leading to system-wide control.
  
- **Google Chrome Global Protect App PE Hole (versions before 6.9)**
  - This vulnerability allows attackers to bypass security measures in the app's PE hole, leading to unauthorized access.

### **Mitigation Recommendations**

1. **Apply Patches Immediately**:
   - Install the latest versions of GlobalProtect App and Google Chrome to patch identified vulnerabilities.

2. **User Training**:
   - Educate users on proper login procedures and awareness of suspicious activities to mitigate risks associated with compromised keys or credentials.

3. **Implement Additional Safeguards**:
   - Use system-wide policies, such as blocking access to the PE hole until patched.
   - Encourage system administrators to patch Chrome thoroughly after GlobalProtect App updates.

4. **Monitor for Updates**:
   - Regularly check for new vulnerabilities and apply patches promptly upon release.

In summary, these vulnerabilities present significant risks to user data and system integrity. Immediate action is required to patch systems and reinforce security measures to prevent potential breaches.

CVE: CVE-2022-0019
Name: GlobalProtect App: Insufficiently Protected Credentials Vulnerability on Linux
Description: An insufficiently protected credentials vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Linux that exposes the hashed credentials of GlobalProtect users that saved their password during previous GlobalProtect app sessions to other local users on the system. The exposed credentials enable a local attacker to authenticate to the GlobalProtect portal or gateway as the target user without knowing of the target users plaintext password. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than and including GlobalProtect app 5.2.7 on Linux. GlobalProtect app 5.3 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux. This issue does not affect the GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 5.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:L/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Linux, GlobalProtect app 5.3.2 on Linux, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

Existing credentials files that are exposed by this issue will be secured when the fixed GlobalProtect app is launched.
Workarounds: 
Users should not save their credentials until the GlobalProtect app is upgraded to a fixed version.

GlobalProtect portal administrators can prevent GlobalProtect app users from saving their credentials on the next connection to the GlobalProtect portal by preventing Save User Credentials from the portal agent configuration as described here:

https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/user-behavior-options.html
CWE IDs: CWE-522

CVE: CVE-2022-0018
Name: GlobalProtect App: Information Exposure Vulnerability When Connecting to GlobalProtect Portal With Single Sign-On Enabled
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in the Palo Alto Networks GlobalProtect app on Windows and MacOS where the credentials of the local user account are sent to the GlobalProtect portal when the Single Sign-On feature is enabled in the GlobalProtect portal configuration. This product behavior is intentional and poses no security risk when connecting to trusted GlobalProtect portals configured to use the same Single Sign-On credentials both for the local user account as well as the GlobalProtect login. However when the credentials are different, the local account credentials are inadvertently sent to the GlobalProtect portal for authentication. A third party MITM type of attacker cannot see these credentials in transit. This vulnerability is a concern where the GlobalProtect app is deployed on Bring-your-Own-Device (BYOD) type of clients with private local user accounts or GlobalProtect app is used to connect to different organizations. Fixed versions of GlobalProtect app have an app setting to prevent the transmission of the user's local user credentials to the target GlobalProtect portal regardless of the portal configuration. This issue impacts: GlobalProtect app 5.1 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS; GlobalProtect app 5.2 versions earlier than GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS This issue does not affect GlobalProtect app on other platforms.
Severity: 6.5 (Medium)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in GlobalProtect app 5.1.10 on Windows and MacOS, GlobalProtect app 5.2.9 on Windows and MacOS, and all later GlobalProtect app versions with the force-disable-sso app setting.

Set force-disable-sso to yes to prevent unintended transmission of the local user credentials as described here:
https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/globalprotect/10-1/globalprotect-admin/globalprotect-apps/deploy-app-settings-transparently/customizable-app-settings/app-behavior-options.html
Workarounds: 
There are no known workarounds for this issue.
CWE IDs: CWE-200

CVE: CVE-2024-8687
Name: PAN-OS: Cleartext Exposure of GlobalProtect Portal Passcodes
Description: An information exposure vulnerability exists in Palo Alto Networks PAN-OS software that enables a GlobalProtect end user to learn both the configured GlobalProtect uninstall password and the configured disable or disconnect passcode. After the password or passcode is known, end users can uninstall, disable, or disconnect GlobalProtect even if the GlobalProtect app configuration would not normally permit them to do so.
Severity: 7.1 (High)
CVSS: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:H
Product: GlobalProtect
Affected Versions: 5.2.5
Mitigation: This issue is fixed in PAN-OS 8.1.25, PAN-OS 9.0.17, PAN-OS 9.1.16, PAN-OS 10.0.12, PAN-OS 10.1.9, PAN-OS 10.2.4, PAN-OS 11.0.1, and all later PAN-OS versions. It is also fixed in Prisma Access 10.2.9 and all later Prisma Access versions. To maintain GlobalProtect app functionality for the vulnerable features, we released a corresponding software update for GlobalProtect app 5.1.12, GlobalProtect app 5.2.13, GlobalProtect app 6.0.7, GlobalProtect app 6.1.2, and GlobalProtect app 6.2.1, and all later GlobalProtect app versions.

To maintain the ability for end users to use the uninstall password feature and the disable or disconnect passcode feature, you must ensure that you upgrade all GlobalProtect app deployments to a fixed version before you upgrade your PAN-OS software to a fixed version.

All fixed versions of GlobalProtect are backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of PAN-OS software. However, fixed versions of PAN-OS software are not backwards compatible with vulnerable versions of GlobalProtect.

You can find additional information for PAN-204689 here:  https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/pan-os/11-1/pan-os-release-notes/pan-os-11-1-0-known-and-addressed-issues/pan-os-11-1-0-known-issues 

Prisma Access customers can open a support case to request an upgrade.
Workarounds: 
Change the following two settings (if enabled) to "Allow with Ticket":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Disable GlobalProtect App
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow user to disconnect GlobalProtect App

Change the following setting (if enabled) to "Disallow":
* Network > GlobalProtect > Portals >  > Agent >  > App > Allow User to Uninstall GlobalProtect App
